\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} may be interpreted as follows\+: Given the prescribed pressure drop \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$ (and thus \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$), we wish to determine an \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape of the required mean \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$ that satisfies the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} along the contact line.\textbackslash{}subsection cartesian Cartesian P\+DE-\/based formulation\+Expressing the (non-\/dimensional) height of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} above the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane as \textbackslash{}f\$ x\+\_\+3 = u(x\+\_\+1,x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$ yields the cartesian form of the Young-\/Laplace \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{equation\+:\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}Delta p = \textbackslash{}kappa = -\/ \textbackslash{}nabla \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}frac\{\textbackslash{}nabla u\}\{\textbackslash{}sqrt\{1+$\vert$\textbackslash{}nabla u$\vert$$^\wedge$2\}\},\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]}where \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}nabla = (\textbackslash{}partial/\textbackslash{}partial x\+\_\+1,\textbackslash{}partial/\textbackslash{}partial x\+\_\+2)$^\wedge$T \textbackslash{}f\$\+Given the imposed pressure drop across the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, this equation must be solved for \textbackslash{}f\$ u(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$. Note that this is only possibleif the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} can be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane. \textbackslash{}subsection pvd The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements\+The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape can also be determinedfrom the $<$A H\+R\+EF=\char`\"{}http\+:principle of virtual displacements$<$/A $>$\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s \textbackslash{}right)=\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}Delta p \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s+\textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{cdot\textbackslash{}delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} l \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} @E\mbox{[}var\+\_\+prin\mbox{]}@\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} which may be derived from energetic considerations. Here the symbol \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}f\$ denotes a variation, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}f\$ is the position vector to the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, and the vector \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}f\$ is the unit normal to the meniscus. The lefthand side of this equation represents the variation of the interfacial energy during a virtual displacement, and \textbackslash{}f\$ ds \textbackslash{}f\$ is an infinitesimal element of the meniscus surface, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$S\textbackslash{}f\$. The terms on the right hand side represent thevirtual work done by the pressure and the virtual work done by thesurface tension forces acting at the free contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}}, respectively. \textbackslash{}f\$ dl \textbackslash{}f\$ is the length of an element of the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{line\textbackslash{}f}} \$L\textbackslash{}f\$, and \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}f\$ is the vector tangent to the interfaceand normal to the contact line. Note that, if the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} is pinned, the variation of its position is zero, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf 0\} \textbackslash{}f\$, and the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} integral vanishes.\+The variational formulation of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} is particularly convenient for a finite-\/element-\/based solution;see, e.\+g. the$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../solid/solid\+\_\+theory/html/index.\+html\#Cartesian\+Lagrangian\char`\"{}$>$Solid Mechanics Theory document$<$/a $>$ for a discussion of howto discretise variational principles with finite elements. Thevariational and P\+DE-\/based formulations are, of course, related to eachother\+:\+The Young-\/Laplace equation is the Euler-\/Lagrange equation of thevariational principle.\textbackslash{}subsection intrinsic Parametric representation To deal with cases in which the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} cannot be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane, we parametrise the meniscus by two intrinsic coordinates as \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$3\textbackslash{}f\$, where \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in D \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$2\textbackslash{}f\$. Furthermore, we parametrise the domain \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}}, \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}partial D\textbackslash{}f\$, by a scalar coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}xi\textbackslash{}f\$ so that, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\{(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}bigg$\vert$\textbackslash{}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\}. \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} The normal to the meniscus is then given by \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}bf N\}=\textbackslash{}frac\{\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 1\} \textbackslash{}times \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 2\} \}\{\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\}, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} where the commas denote partial differentiation with respect to theintrinsic coordinates, and \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}=$\vert$\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 1\} \textbackslash{}times \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 2\}$\vert$\textbackslash{}f\$ is the square root of the surface metric tensor.\+The area and length differentials required in variational \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{principleare\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}d s=\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2 \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} and \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}d l=\textbackslash{}left$\vert$\textbackslash{}frac\{d \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right)\}\{d \textbackslash{}xi\} \textbackslash{}right$\vert$d \textbackslash{}xi,\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} allowing us to write the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{as\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}frac\{\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\}\{\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\} -\/\textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2=\textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}left$\vert$\textbackslash{}frac\{d \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right)\}\{d \textbackslash{}xi\} \textbackslash{}right$\vert$d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{xi.\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{]}\textbackslash{}subsection \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} The method of spines\+In the current form, the variational \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} cannot yielda unique solution because there are infinitely many vector fields \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$ that parametrisethe same \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape. To remove this ambiguity, and to allow for \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shapes that cannot be projected onto the\textbackslash{}f\$(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane, we employ the so-\/called \char`\"{}Method of Spines\char`\"{}.This method was originally proposed by Kistler and Scrivenfor the computation of free surface flows. We decompose the vector \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{}f\$ into two parts by writing it as \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)+\textbackslash{}mathit\{u\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2). \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} Here the \char`\"{}spine basis\char`\"{} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$and the \char`\"{}spines\char`\"{} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ are pre-\/determined vectorfields that must be chosen by the user. Using thisdecomposition, the meniscus shape is determined by the scalar function\textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}mathit\{u\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ which represents the meniscus\textquotesingle{} displacement along the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf S\}\textbackslash{}f\$.\+The idea is illustrated in the simple 2D sketch below\+:the spinebasis vectors, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}zeta), \textbackslash{}f\$ parametrise the straight \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} corresponding to a flat meniscus. Positive values of \textbackslash{}f\$ u \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$displace the meniscus along the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}}, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}zeta) \textbackslash{}f\$(the red vectors), whose orientation allows the representation of meniscus shapes that cannot be represented in cartesian form as \textbackslash{}f\$ x\+\_\+2=u(x\+\_\+1). \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+35\textbackslash{}textwidth spine\+\_\+sketch \char`\"{}Sketch illustrating the parametrisation of the meniscus by the Method of Spines. \char`\"{}The spine basis and the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} themselves must be chosen such that the mapping from \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ to \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ isone-\/to-\/\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}}, at least for the meniscus shapesof interest. Pinned \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} of the form\textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}rm pinned\} \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$are most easily imposed by choosing the spine basis such that \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. \{\textbackslash{}bfB\}\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}rm pinned\}, \textbackslash{}f\$ implyingthat \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. u\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=0. \textbackslash{}f\$ The simplest possible choice for the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} and spine basisis \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}} that returns the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} to its original cartesian formulation.\+This is achieved by setting \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2, 0)$^\wedge$T \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=(0, 0, 1)$^\wedge$T. \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}subsection displ Displacement Control\+The Young-\/Laplace equation is a highly nonlinear P\+D\+E. We therefore require a good initial guess for the solution in order to ensure theconvergence of the Newton iteration. In many cases good initial guesses can beprovided by a simple, physically motivated continuation method.\+For instance in the model \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} shown above, the computation wasstarted by computing the solution for \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p=\textbackslash{}kappa=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ -\/-\/a flat interface. This solution was then used as the initial guess for the solution at a small positive value of \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$. This processwas continued, allowing us to compute strongly deformedmeniscus shapes. This method works well, provided small increments in the control parameter \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$(or equivalently, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$) create small changes in the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape. This is not alwaysthe case, however, as we shall see in the example below. In such cases it is often possible to re-\/formulate the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}}, using the displacement control method discussed in the$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../beam/steady\+\_\+ring/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$solidmechanics tutorials$<$/a $>$. Rather than prescribing the pressure drop \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$ we prescribe the displacement of a control point on the meniscus andregard the pressure drop required to achieve this displacementas an unknown. Since the implementation of the method is very similarto that used for solid mechanics \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ae8d86658dc1ec3aa7122edd47ef4124e}{problems}}, we shall notdiscuss it in detail here but refer to the appropriate$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../beam/steady\+\_\+ring/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$solid mechanics tutorial.$<$/a $>$$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$\textbackslash{}section barrel An example problem\+:A barrel-\/shaped meniscus\+As an example, we consider the following problem\+:\+Fluid is extrudedfrom an infinitely long, parallel-\/sided slot of width \textbackslash{}f\$ 2a \textbackslash{}f\$.\+If we assume that the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} is pinned at the edges ofthe slot, as shown in the sketch below, the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} has an obvious exact solution. The air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} must have constant mean \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}}, so, assuming that its shape does not vary along the slot, the meniscus must be a circularcylinder. If we characterise the meniscus\textquotesingle{} shape by its verticaldisplacement along the centreline, \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$, the(dimensional) \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} of the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} is given \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{by\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$=\textbackslash{}frac\{2/a\}\{H/a+a/H\}.\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} The plot of this function, shown in the right half of the figurebelow, may be interpreted as a \char`\"{}load-\/displacementdiagram\char`\"{} as it shows the deflection of the meniscus as a function of the imposed non-\/dimensional pressure drop across the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p=a \textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$. \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth meniscus\+\_\+sketch\+\_\+and\+\_\+limit\+\_\+point \char`\"{}Sketch of the meniscus above a slot of width 2a. The figure on the right illustrates the relation between the meniscus \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} and its vertical displacement along the centreline. \char`\"{}The plot shows that the load-\/displacement curve is not single-\/valued. Furthermore, the presence of a limit point at \textbackslash{}f\$ a \textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$=1 \textbackslash{}f\$ indicates that the maximum \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} of the meniscus is given by \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa\+\_\+\{max\}$^\wedge$ $\ast$=1/a. \textbackslash{}f\$ This implies that the maximum(dimensional) pressure that the meniscus canwithstand is given by \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p$^\wedge$ $\ast$\+\_\+\{max\}=\textbackslash{}sigma \textbackslash{}kappa\+\_\+\{max\}$^\wedge$ $\ast$=\textbackslash{}sigma/a \textbackslash{}f\$.\+The presence of the limit point makes it impossible to compute the entire solution curve by simply increasing \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$ in small increments. However, use of a displacement control approach, by prescribing \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$ while regarding \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$(and thus \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}kappa\textbackslash{}f\$) as an unknown, yields a single-\/valued function that can be computed by a straightforward continuation method in which \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$ is increased in small increments. This approach was employed to compute the meniscus shapes shown in the plot below. The initial, zero-\/\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} configurationof the meniscus(corresponding to a vanishing pressure drop across the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}) is the unit square. The meniscus is pinned along the lines \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1 \textbackslash{}f\$, and symmetry(natural) \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} were applied along the lines \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a972796dc0dbb3f5b13cbc503572d2a26}{x}}=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a972796dc0dbb3f5b13cbc503572d2a26}{x}}=1;\textbackslash{}f\$ see \textbackslash{}ref comm\+\_\+ex for further details on the natural \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} conditions.\+As the pressure drop increases, the meniscus is deflected upwardsuntil it reaches the configuration of maximum \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} when \textbackslash{}f\$ H/a=1 \textbackslash{}f\$. Beyond this point, the pressure drop has to be reducedto compute the \char`\"{}bulging\char`\"{} meniscus shapes obtained for \textbackslash{}f\$ H/a $>$ 1. \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth barrel \char`\"{}Deformation of a meniscus that is pinned along the lines \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 and \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1. \char`\"{}The comparison of the computed \char`\"{}load-\/displacement curve\char`\"{} against the exact solution, shown below, indicates that the two agreeto within plotting accuracy. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace \char`\"{}Load-\/displacement diagram for a meniscus that is pinned along the lines \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 and \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1. \char`\"{}$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}section impl Implementation\+We shall now discuss the solution of the above \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} with\textbackslash{}c oomph-\/lib \textquotesingle{}s Young Laplace elements.\textbackslash{}subsection namespace The global namespace\+As usual we define the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} parameters in a global namespace.\+The key parameter is the value of the prescribed control displacementwhich we initialise to zero. the interfacial forces acting at the air liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} I w textwidth spherical\+\_\+cap A typical $\ast$,\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} where \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} kappa \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} sigma \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} the surface tension Non dimensionalising Delta p yields the non dimensional form of the Young Laplace equation \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}Delta p=\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{kappa.\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{]} This must be augmented by suitable \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} to be applied at the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} along which the meniscus meets the solid surface We can either pin the position of the contact or prescribe the$<$ A H\+R\+EF=\char`\"{}http\+:angle$<$/A$>$ at which the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} meets the solid surface.\+The mathematical \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} may be interpreted as follows\+: Given the prescribed pressure drop \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$ (and thus \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$), we wish to determine an \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape of the required mean \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$ that satisfies the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} along the contact line.\textbackslash{}subsection cartesian Cartesian P\+DE-\/based formulation\+Expressing the (non-\/dimensional) height of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} above the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane as \textbackslash{}f\$ x\+\_\+3 = u(x\+\_\+1,x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$ yields the cartesian form of the Young-\/Laplace \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{equation\+:\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}Delta p = \textbackslash{}kappa = -\/ \textbackslash{}nabla \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}frac\{\textbackslash{}nabla u\}\{\textbackslash{}sqrt\{1+$\vert$\textbackslash{}nabla u$\vert$$^\wedge$2\}\},\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]}where \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}nabla = (\textbackslash{}partial/\textbackslash{}partial x\+\_\+1,\textbackslash{}partial/\textbackslash{}partial x\+\_\+2)$^\wedge$T \textbackslash{}f\$\+Given the imposed pressure drop across the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, this equation must be solved for \textbackslash{}f\$ u(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$. Note that this is only possibleif the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} can be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane. \textbackslash{}subsection pvd The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements\+The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape can also be determinedfrom the $<$A H\+R\+EF=\char`\"{}http\+:principle of virtual displacements$<$/A $>$\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s \textbackslash{}right)=\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}Delta p \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s+\textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{cdot\textbackslash{}delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} l \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} @E\mbox{[}var\+\_\+prin\mbox{]}@\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} which may be derived from energetic considerations. Here the symbol \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}f\$ denotes a variation, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}f\$ is the position vector to the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, and the vector \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}f\$ is the unit normal to the meniscus. The lefthand side of this equation represents the variation of the interfacial energy during a virtual displacement, and \textbackslash{}f\$ ds \textbackslash{}f\$ is an infinitesimal element of the meniscus surface, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$S\textbackslash{}f\$. The terms on the right hand side represent thevirtual work done by the pressure and the virtual work done by thesurface tension forces acting at the free contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}}, respectively. \textbackslash{}f\$ dl \textbackslash{}f\$ is the length of an element of the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{line\textbackslash{}f}} \$L\textbackslash{}f\$, and \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}f\$ is the vector tangent to the interfaceand normal to the contact line. Note that, if the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} is pinned, the variation of its position is zero, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf 0\} \textbackslash{}f\$, and the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} integral vanishes.\+The variational formulation of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} is particularly convenient for a finite-\/element-\/based solution;see, e.\+g. the$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../solid/solid\+\_\+theory/html/index.\+html\#Cartesian\+Lagrangian\char`\"{}$>$Solid Mechanics Theory document$<$/a $>$ for a discussion of howto discretise variational principles with finite elements. Thevariational and P\+DE-\/based formulations are, of course, related to eachother\+:\+The Young-\/Laplace equation is the Euler-\/Lagrange equation of thevariational principle.\textbackslash{}subsection intrinsic Parametric representation To deal with cases in which the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} cannot be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane, we parametrise the meniscus by two intrinsic coordinates as \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$3\textbackslash{}f\$, where \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in D \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$2\textbackslash{}f\$. Furthermore, we parametrise the domain \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}}, \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}partial D\textbackslash{}f\$, by a scalar coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}xi\textbackslash{}f\$ so that, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\{(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}bigg$\vert$\textbackslash{}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\}. \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} The normal to the meniscus is then given by \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}bf N\}=\textbackslash{}frac\{\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 1\} \textbackslash{}times \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 2\} \}\{\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\}, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} where the commas denote partial differentiation with respect to theintrinsic coordinates, and \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}=$\vert$\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 1\} \textbackslash{}times \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{, 2\}$\vert$\textbackslash{}f\$ is the square root of the surface metric tensor.\+The area and length differentials required in variational \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{principleare\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}d s=\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2 \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} and \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}d l=\textbackslash{}left$\vert$\textbackslash{}frac\{d \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right)\}\{d \textbackslash{}xi\} \textbackslash{}right$\vert$d \textbackslash{}xi,\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} allowing us to write the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{as\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}frac\{\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\}\{\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\} -\/\textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2=\textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}left$\vert$\textbackslash{}frac\{d \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right)\}\{d \textbackslash{}xi\} \textbackslash{}right$\vert$d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{xi.\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{]}\textbackslash{}subsection \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} The method of spines\+In the current form, the variational \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} cannot yielda unique solution because there are infinitely many vector fields \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$ that parametrisethe same \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape. To remove this ambiguity, and to allow for \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shapes that cannot be projected onto the\textbackslash{}f\$(x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane, we employ the so-\/called \char`\"{}Method of Spines\char`\"{}.This method was originally proposed by Kistler and Scrivenfor the computation of free surface flows. We decompose the vector \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{}f\$ into two parts by writing it as \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)+\textbackslash{}mathit\{u\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2). \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} Here the \char`\"{}spine basis\char`\"{} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$and the \char`\"{}spines\char`\"{} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ are pre-\/determined vectorfields that must be chosen by the user. Using thisdecomposition, the meniscus shape is determined by the scalar function\textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}mathit\{u\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ which represents the meniscus\textquotesingle{} displacement along the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf S\}\textbackslash{}f\$.\+The idea is illustrated in the simple 2D sketch below\+:the spinebasis vectors, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}zeta), \textbackslash{}f\$ parametrise the straight \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} corresponding to a flat meniscus. Positive values of \textbackslash{}f\$ u \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$displace the meniscus along the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}}, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}zeta) \textbackslash{}f\$(the red vectors), whose orientation allows the representation of meniscus shapes that cannot be represented in cartesian form as \textbackslash{}f\$ x\+\_\+2=u(x\+\_\+1). \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+35\textbackslash{}textwidth spine\+\_\+sketch \char`\"{}Sketch illustrating the parametrisation of the meniscus by the Method of Spines. \char`\"{}The spine basis and the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} themselves must be chosen such that the mapping from \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ to \textbackslash{}f\$\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}f\$ isone-\/to-\/\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}}, at least for the meniscus shapesof interest. Pinned \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} of the form\textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}rm pinned\} \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$are most easily imposed by choosing the spine basis such that \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. \{\textbackslash{}bfB\}\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}rm pinned\}, \textbackslash{}f\$ implyingthat \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}left. u\textbackslash{}right$\vert$\+\_\+\{\textbackslash{}partial D\}=0. \textbackslash{}f\$ The simplest possible choice for the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} and spine basisis \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}} that returns the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} to its original cartesian formulation.\+This is achieved by setting \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2, 0)$^\wedge$T \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=(0, 0, 1)$^\wedge$T. \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}subsection displ Displacement Control\+The Young-\/Laplace equation is a highly nonlinear P\+D\+E. We therefore require a good initial guess for the solution in order to ensure theconvergence of the Newton iteration. In many cases good initial guesses can beprovided by a simple, physically motivated continuation method.\+For instance in the model \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} shown above, the computation wasstarted by computing the solution for \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p=\textbackslash{}kappa=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ -\/-\/a flat interface. This solution was then used as the initial guess for the solution at a small positive value of \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$. This processwas continued, allowing us to compute strongly deformedmeniscus shapes. This method works well, provided small increments in the control parameter \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$(or equivalently, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$) create small changes in the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape. This is not alwaysthe case, however, as we shall see in the example below. In such cases it is often possible to re-\/formulate the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}}, using the displacement control method discussed in the$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../beam/steady\+\_\+ring/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$solidmechanics tutorials$<$/a $>$. Rather than prescribing the pressure drop \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$ we prescribe the displacement of a control point on the meniscus andregard the pressure drop required to achieve this displacementas an unknown. Since the implementation of the method is very similarto that used for solid mechanics \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ae8d86658dc1ec3aa7122edd47ef4124e}{problems}}, we shall notdiscuss it in detail here but refer to the appropriate$<$ a href=\char`\"{}../../../beam/steady\+\_\+ring/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$solid mechanics tutorial.$<$/a $>$$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$\textbackslash{}section barrel An example problem\+:A barrel-\/shaped meniscus\+As an example, we consider the following problem\+:\+Fluid is extrudedfrom an infinitely long, parallel-\/sided slot of width \textbackslash{}f\$ 2a \textbackslash{}f\$.\+If we assume that the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} is pinned at the edges ofthe slot, as shown in the sketch below, the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} has an obvious exact solution. The air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} must have constant mean \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}}, so, assuming that its shape does not vary along the slot, the meniscus must be a circularcylinder. If we characterise the meniscus\textquotesingle{} shape by its verticaldisplacement along the centreline, \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$, the(dimensional) \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} of the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} is given \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{by\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$=\textbackslash{}frac\{2/a\}\{H/a+a/H\}.\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]} The plot of this function, shown in the right half of the figurebelow, may be interpreted as a \char`\"{}load-\/displacementdiagram\char`\"{} as it shows the deflection of the meniscus as a function of the imposed non-\/dimensional pressure drop across the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p=a \textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$. \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth meniscus\+\_\+sketch\+\_\+and\+\_\+limit\+\_\+point \char`\"{}Sketch of the meniscus above a slot of width 2a. The figure on the right illustrates the relation between the meniscus \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} and its vertical displacement along the centreline. \char`\"{}The plot shows that the load-\/displacement curve is not single-\/valued. Furthermore, the presence of a limit point at \textbackslash{}f\$ a \textbackslash{}kappa$^\wedge$ $\ast$=1 \textbackslash{}f\$ indicates that the maximum \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} of the meniscus is given by \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa\+\_\+\{max\}$^\wedge$ $\ast$=1/a. \textbackslash{}f\$ This implies that the maximum(dimensional) pressure that the meniscus canwithstand is given by \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p$^\wedge$ $\ast$\+\_\+\{max\}=\textbackslash{}sigma \textbackslash{}kappa\+\_\+\{max\}$^\wedge$ $\ast$=\textbackslash{}sigma/a \textbackslash{}f\$.\+The presence of the limit point makes it impossible to compute the entire solution curve by simply increasing \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{}f\$ in small increments. However, use of a displacement control approach, by prescribing \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$ while regarding \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}Delta p \textbackslash{}f\$(and thus \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}kappa\textbackslash{}f\$) as an unknown, yields a single-\/valued function that can be computed by a straightforward continuation method in which \textbackslash{}f\$ H \textbackslash{}f\$ is increased in small increments. This approach was employed to compute the meniscus shapes shown in the plot below. The initial, zero-\/\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} configurationof the meniscus(corresponding to a vanishing pressure drop across the air-\/liquid \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}) is the unit square. The meniscus is pinned along the lines \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1 \textbackslash{}f\$, and symmetry(natural) \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a7f08e15ca2e78d4f74694e3111124596}{conditions}} were applied along the lines \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a972796dc0dbb3f5b13cbc503572d2a26}{x}}=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ and \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} \$\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a972796dc0dbb3f5b13cbc503572d2a26}{x}}=1;\textbackslash{}f\$ see \textbackslash{}ref comm\+\_\+ex for further details on the natural \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}} conditions.\+As the pressure drop increases, the meniscus is deflected upwardsuntil it reaches the configuration of maximum \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} when \textbackslash{}f\$ H/a=1 \textbackslash{}f\$. Beyond this point, the pressure drop has to be reducedto compute the \char`\"{}bulging\char`\"{} meniscus shapes obtained for \textbackslash{}f\$ H/a $>$ 1. \textbackslash{}f\$ @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth barrel \char`\"{}Deformation of a meniscus that is pinned along the lines \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 and \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1. \char`\"{}The comparison of the computed \char`\"{}load-\/displacement curve\char`\"{} against the exact solution, shown below, indicates that the two agreeto within plotting accuracy. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace \char`\"{}Load-\/displacement diagram for a meniscus that is pinned along the lines \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=0 and \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}=1. \char`\"{}$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}section impl Implementation\+We shall now discuss the solution of the above \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} with\textbackslash{}c oomph-\/lib \textquotesingle{}s Young Laplace elements.\textbackslash{}subsection namespace The global namespace\+As usual we define the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} parameters in a global namespace.\+The key parameter is the value of the prescribed control displacementwhich we initialise to zero. The function \textbackslash{}c get\+\_\+exact\+\_\+kappa() returns the exact solution for the mean \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} of the meniscus.\+We will use this function for the validation of our results.\textbackslash{}dontinclude barrel.\+cc\textbackslash{}skipline start\+\_\+of\+\_\+namespace\textbackslash{}until end exact kappa Next we define the orientation of the spines. Anticipating the shapeof the meniscus, we set \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf B\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2, 0) \textbackslash{}f\$ so that \textbackslash{}f\$ u=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ corresponds to a flatmeniscus in the \textbackslash{}f\$(\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a972796dc0dbb3f5b13cbc503572d2a26}{x}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane,\textbackslash{}until bspine functionsand rotate the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} in the \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1ed379f41acee082a02b9ce12b741bd6}{direction}} by \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{setting\textbackslash{}f}}\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}bf S\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\textbackslash{}left(\textbackslash{}begin\{array\}\{c\}0 \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}-\/\textbackslash{}sin\textbackslash{}big(\textbackslash{}alpha(\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}big) \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}cos\textbackslash{}big(\textbackslash{}alpha(\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)\textbackslash{}big) \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}end\{array\}\textbackslash{}right)\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}}\mbox{]}where \textbackslash{}alpha(\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2)=\textbackslash{}alpha\+\_\+\{min\}+(\textbackslash{}alpha\+\_\+\{max\}-\/\textbackslash{}alpha\+\_\+\{min\})\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2 \textbackslash{}f\$. With this choice, the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_aeca3fbb0467bbb9f89ebed58aa1c7ffa}{spines}} are unit vectors thatform an angle \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}alpha \textbackslash{}f\$(varying between \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}alpha\+\_\+\{min\} \textbackslash{}f\$ and\textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}alpha\+\_\+\{max\} \textbackslash{}f\$) with the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1b792a58562211eb74439f1222d226a4}{y}}-\/axis.\textbackslash{}until spine function$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$\textbackslash{}subsection \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8cc_a0ddf1224851353fc92bfbff6f499fa97}{main}} The driver code\+We start by preparing an output directory and open a trace file to record the control displacement, and the computed andexact values of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} barrel.\+cc\textbackslash{}skipline start\+\_\+of\+\_\+main \textbackslash{}until Z\+O\+N\+E\+Next we build the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} object increments and re-\/computing the meniscus shapes and the associated \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} curvatures.\textbackslash{}until end of \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8cc_a0ddf1224851353fc92bfbff6f499fa97}{main}}$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$\textbackslash{}subsection class The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} class\+The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} class has the usual member functions.(Ignore the linesin \textbackslash{}c actions\+\_\+before\+\_\+newton\+\_\+solve() as they are irrelevant in thecurrent context. They are discussed in \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}} of the exercises in \textbackslash{}ref comm\+\_\+ex.) The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} \textquotesingle{}s private memberdata include a pointer to the node at which the meniscus displacementis controlled by the displacement control element, and a pointer to the \textbackslash{}c Data object whose \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a0cc3d24c53996627ec3a5cd70d7d0eb7}{one}}-\/and-\/only value contains the unknowninterface \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}}, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}kappa. \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}dontinclude barrel.\+cc\textbackslash{}skipline start\+\_\+of\+\_\+problem\+\_\+class\textbackslash{}until end of \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}}$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$\textbackslash{}subsection constr The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} constructor\+We start by building the mesh, discretising the two-\/dimensionalparameter space \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in\mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]} \textbackslash{}times\mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}\textbackslash{}f\$ with 8x8 elements.\textbackslash{}until mesh\+\_\+pt() Next, we choose the central node in the mesh as the node whosedisplacement is imposed by the displacement control method. \textbackslash{}until Control\+\_\+node\+\_\+pt-\/$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} kappa \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a9ac1b72ad803292913ca4f9bc7ac1189}{f}} We store the pointer to this c Data object in the private member data to facilitate its output until and the prescribed \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a6a63e58ac8fc8170c7517d6c91561372}{curvature}} until \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_afd7bfc074226d266df4e6c70265af3c9}{Finally}}
\item

Note that this is only possibleif the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} can be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane. \textbackslash{}subsection pvd The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements\+The \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} shape can also be determinedfrom the $<$A H\+R\+EF=\char`\"{}http\+:principle of virtual displacements$<$/A$>$\textbackslash{}f\mbox{[} \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}left( \textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s \textbackslash{}right)= \textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}Delta p \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} s + \textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{cdot\textbackslash{}delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}mathit\{\textbackslash{}, d\} l \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{} @E\mbox{[}var\+\_\+prin\mbox{]}@\textbackslash{}f\mbox{]} which may be derived from energetic considerations. Here the symbol \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}f\$ denotes a variation, \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R \} \textbackslash{}f\$ is the position vector to the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}}, and the vector \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf N\}\textbackslash{}f\$ is the unit normal to the meniscus. The lefthand side of this equation represents the variation of the interfacial energy during a virtual displacement, and \textbackslash{}f\$ ds \textbackslash{}f\$ is an infinitesimal element of the meniscus surface, \textbackslash{}f\$\+S\textbackslash{}f\$. The terms on the right hand side represent thevirtual work done by the pressure and the virtual work done by thesurface tension forces acting at the free contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}}, respectively. \textbackslash{}f\$ dl \textbackslash{}f\$ is the length of an element of the contact line\textbackslash{}f\$\+L\textbackslash{}f\$, and \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}f\$ is the vector tangent to the interfaceand normal to the contact line. Note that, if the contact \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} is pinned, the variation of its position is zero, \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} = \{\textbackslash{}bf 0\} \textbackslash{}f\$, and the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a72be276e8168a9e3345791225137a522}{line}} integral vanishes.\+The variational formulation of the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a8044b62475f8b6be7b371532bab17017}{problem}} is particularly convenient for a finite-\/element-\/based solution; see, e.\+g. the$<$a href=\char`\"{}../../../solid/solid\+\_\+theory/html/index.\+html\#Cartesian\+Lagrangian\char`\"{}$>$Solid Mechanics Theory document$<$/a$>$ for a discussion of howto discretise variational principles with finite elements. Thevariational and P\+DE-\/based formulations are, of course, related to eachother\+: The Young-\/Laplace equation is the Euler-\/Lagrange equation of thevariational principle.\textbackslash{}subsection intrinsic Parametric representation To deal with cases in which the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a5ea2ccd2302f3ef85d1dc917d935b659}{interface}} cannot be projected onto the \textbackslash{}f\$ (x\+\_\+1, x\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}f\$-\/plane, we parametrise the meniscus by two intrinsic coordinates as \textbackslash{}f\$ \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$3\textbackslash{}f\$, where \textbackslash{}f\$(\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) \textbackslash{}in D \textbackslash{}in \{ R\}$^\wedge$2\textbackslash{}f\$. Furthermore, we parametrise the domain \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a1c89605709bfb613fd19c9f098dd6eda}{boundary}}, \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}partial D\textbackslash{}f\$, by a scalar coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$\textbackslash{}xi\textbackslash{}f\$ so that, \textbackslash{}f\mbox{[}\{\textbackslash{}partial D\} = \textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\{ (\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}},\textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2) = \textbackslash{}left( \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}bigg\textbackslash{}\}. \textbackslash{}f\mbox{]} The normal to the meniscus is then given by \textbackslash{}f\mbox{[} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} = \textbackslash{}frac\{\{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\+\_\+\{,1\} \textbackslash{}times \{\textbackslash{}bf the square root of the surface metric tensor.\+The area and length differentials required in variational principleare\textbackslash{}f\mbox{[} d s=\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2 \textbackslash{}f\mbox{]} and \textbackslash{}f\mbox{[} d l=\textbackslash{}left$\vert$ \textbackslash{}frac\{d \{\textbackslash{}bf R\}\textbackslash{}left( \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{} \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi) \textbackslash{}right)\}\{d \textbackslash{}xi\} \textbackslash{}right$\vert$ d \textbackslash{}xi,\textbackslash{}f\mbox{]} allowing us to write the \mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a4919b2fccf0613c276d0ca7bfbf41441}{principle}} of virtual displacements as\textbackslash{}f\mbox{[} \textbackslash{}int\+\_\+S \textbackslash{}left( \textbackslash{}frac\{\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\}\{\textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\}\} -\/\textbackslash{}kappa \textbackslash{} \{\textbackslash{}bf N\} \textbackslash{}cdot \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_ab527d223c14587f4aebca609ce74db8a}{delta}} \{\textbackslash{}bf R\} \textbackslash{}right) \textbackslash{}mathcal\{A\}$^\wedge$\{1/2\} d \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}} d \textbackslash{}zeta\+\_\+2 =\textbackslash{}oint\+\_\+\{L\} \{\textbackslash{}bf T\}\+\_\+n \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{young__laplace_8txt_a89176c66757d666599a5b244526ae379}{zeta\+\_\+1}}$^\wedge$\{\mbox{[}\textbackslash{}partial D\mbox{]}\}(\textbackslash{}xi), \textbackslash{}
